<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_00109b89-b50b-41f3-a53d-94be28630474'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText12462404690005483306" style="display:none">Enter a powerful realm of legend, dark sorcery, and conquest, where the mighty Drenai warrior Druss faces his most deadly opponent . . .<br /><br />Druss the Legend, the dark axman known as the Deathwalker, must join the warrior Talisman on a mission of blood and glory. Only the stolen Eyes of Alchazzar--mystic jewels of power--will save Druss's dying friend, then unite the Nadir tribes against the evil of the Gothir. Druss agrees to help look for the twin gems--hidden for centuries in the shrine of Oshikai, the Demon-bane, the Nadir's greatest hero.<br /><br />It has been prophesied that with the recovery of the stones, there will come the Uniter, a magnificent fighter who will free the Nadir from brutal oppression. But Garen-Tsen, the sadistic power behind the Gothir throne, also seeks the gems. To control them, he will send five thousand men against a handful of savages, Talisman, and the one Drenai warrior.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/419528-does-this-series-need-to-be-read-in-order">Does this series need to be read in order?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_419528'><a id="like_count_community_question_419528" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/419528?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F613994.The_Legend_of_Deathwalker">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2278579-heather-foy"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1465101570i/2278579._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2278579-heather-foy">Heather Foy</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No, you don't *have* to. While the books do mention events and people from the other books, each one stands alone, although I imagine it might be a bi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No, you don't *have* to. While the books do mention events and people from the other books, each one stands alone, although I imagine it might be a bit confusing if you don't know the timeline jumps around. I am currently reading the series in chronological order (based on the timeline in the Drenai world) because I am new to the books, but the books were not originally written in this order. Legend was the first one Gemmell wrote, but it is the 7th chronologically. <br /><br />If you intend to read the entire series, my recommendation would be to read them in Drenai-calendar chronological order though - starting with Waylander. You can find the order here (goodreads numbers them in the order they were written): <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drenai_Series#Chronologyhttp://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drenai_Series#Chronology">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drenai_S...</a><br /><br /> <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1636715340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10603138964910087303">The Legend of Deathwalker (The Drenai Saga, #7), David Gemmell<br/><br/><b>The Legend of Deathwalker</b> is a heroic fantasy novel written by British author <b>David Gemmell</b>, it was first published in 1996. <br/><br/><b>The Legend of Deathwalker</b> is the 7th book released in the <b>Drenai Series</b>. The book details the life of the character <b>Druss</b> and is set chronologically after the main events in <b>The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend</b> but prior to events in Legend. <br/><br/>The novel begins during the defense of the fortress Dros Delnoch fr</span>
  <span id="freeText10603138964910087303" style="display:none">The Legend of Deathwalker (The Drenai Saga, #7), David Gemmell<br /><br /><b>The Legend of Deathwalker</b> is a heroic fantasy novel written by British author <b>David Gemmell</b>, it was first published in 1996. <br /><br /><b>The Legend of Deathwalker</b> is the 7th book released in the <b>Drenai Series</b>. The book details the life of the character <b>Druss</b> and is set chronologically after the main events in <b>The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend</b> but prior to events in Legend. <br /><br />The novel begins during the defense of the fortress Dros Delnoch from the Nadir, Druss begins to tell a young warrior a story from his past. He tells how he and his friend Sieben traveled to the land of the Gothir and how he became involved in the political affairs there. Owing to a prophecy that the King made, Druss must lose a tournament; when he refuses to do this men are hired to kill him. In the course of the attempt on his life his friend Klay is shot in the spine with a crossbow leaving him paralyzed and mortally wounded. <br /><br />To help him Druss travels to the land of the Nadir where a mystic has told him there are gems that can heal any wound. As he travels to the shrine of Nadir hero Oshikai, the Gothir send a force of 2,000 men to destroy it. Druss arrives at the shrine hoping to find the jewels but is unable to do so before the Gothir arrive, and so he helps four Nadir tribes defend the shrine under the guidance of a Gothir-trained Nadir soldier called Talisman. Talisman is on a quest to find "The Uniter", a man with blazing violet eyes called Ulric, who will unite the Nadir tribes after centuries of warfare. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش روز پنجم ماه ژانویه سال 2020 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: افسانه مرگ پیما؛ نویسنده دیوید گمل ؛ مترجم سیدسجاد حامدحیدری؛ تهران: کتابسرای تندیس‏‫، 1398؛ در 440ص؛ شابک 9786001825750؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده 20م<br /><br />دراس اسطوره، تبردار تاریکی، که با نام «مرگ‌ پیما» شناخته می‌شود، باید در مسیر ماموریتی، از برای خون، و از برای افتخار، به جنگجو «تالیسمان» بپیوندد؛ تنها «چشمان الچازار مسروقه- جواهرات افسانه‌ ای جادویی» می‌تواند، دوست در حال مرگ «دراس» را نجات دهد، و سپس قبیله‌ های «نادیر» را، در برابر شرارت «گوتیر»ها متحد کند؛ «دراس» با جستجو برای پیدا کردن جواهراتی که سده هاست در گور «اشیکای اهریمن‌کش»، بزرگ‌ترین قهرمان «نادیر»، پنهان شده، موافقت می‌کند؛ پیشگویی شده، که با پیدا شدن سنگ‌ها، متحد کننده‌ ای خواهد آمد، جنگجویی بی نظیر، که «نادیر»ها را، از ظلم وستم «گوتیر»ها، رها خواهد ساخت؛ اما «گارن_تسن»، نخست وزیر روانی، که قدرت کشور «گوتیر» را، در دستان خویش دارد نیز، به دنبال همان جواهرات است؛ او هم برای بدست آوردن آن‌ جواهرات، دو هزار سرباز مسلح، و آموزش دیده را، به جنگ تعداد کمی وحشی «تالیسمان» و یک جنگجوی «درنای» می‌فرستد؛ <br /><br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2470949369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2470949369" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2470949369?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2470949369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12565610155750664025"><b>A book that grasps the reader at the first sentence and does not let them go until the last page.</b><br/><br/>“Legend of Deathwalker” is the seventh volume in the history of the Drenai. The action of this novel takes place between the events described in the “The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend” and “Legend.” Druss, once again will have to face the destiny and undertake a dangerous quest to save his friend.<br/><br/><b>While Druss will always have a special place for me, in this book he has been dwarfed by another p</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12565610155750664025" style="display:none"><b>A book that grasps the reader at the first sentence and does not let them go until the last page.</b><br /><br />“Legend of Deathwalker” is the seventh volume in the history of the Drenai. The action of this novel takes place between the events described in the “The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend” and “Legend.” Druss, once again will have to face the destiny and undertake a dangerous quest to save his friend.<br /><br /><b>While Druss will always have a special place for me, in this book he has been dwarfed by another protagonist: Talisman.</b> I bet that Mr Gemmell modelled him on a real-life character; figure dark and surrounded by even darker myths. Analogies to the Vlad the Impaler, known more widely as Vlad Dracula, were apparent to me. Vlad, just like Talisman, was taken captive to the hostile state (the Ottoman Empire) in his childhood. This was meant to a guarantee that his father would never attack the sultan's authority. Talisman also goes to the elite military school where he turns out to be a talented strategist and a warrior (Vlad trained with the Janissaries). Anyone who would like to explore the history of the prince transformed into a vampire by Bram Stoker should read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29221047.Vlad_III_Dracula_The_true_story_of_Dracula__the_Impaler" title="Vlad III Dracula The true story of Dracula, the Impaler by Art Mason" rel="nofollow noopener">Vlad III Dracula: The true story of Dracula, the Impaler</a>.<br /><br />Back to the novel at hand. <b>We have everything here: a crazy emperor, lost artefacts with healing powers, ghosts of long-dead heroes, fights, political machinations, more fights…</b> Sometimes it feels a bit too much. Especially, the magic and miracles department is well endowed. <b>I like Mr Gemmell a lot more when the heroes have to rely only on themselves and their strength or cunning</b> instead of waiting for a lightning from heaven or sudden recovery are very much like <i>deus ex machina</i> solutions. I have had the impression that <b>the Author either ran out of ideas halfway through or had too many of them</b> and did not manage to work them neatly into one coherent piece.<br /><br />Still, it is not a bad novel. It <b>fills some gaps in the Drenai history</b>: where did the greatest Nadir commander come from? How did he manage to unite his people? Who was he before he became famous? <b>If Mr Gemmell developed these threads and gave up on the miracles, my rating would be higher</b>.<br /><br />It is my seventh Drenai novel and <b>it is difficult to find something new</b> in this book. Mr Gemmell uses the same schemes, tropes, and arc. However, what is surprising is that <b>despite certain repetitiveness, I always read Mr Gemmell’s books with real pleasure</b>. I recommend the Drenai saga, but I cannot say that this is the finest specimen in the series. Or maybe it is. Read it, and let me know what you think.<br /><br /><i>Note on the rating: 3,5 rounded to 4 stars (for Druss).</i><br /><br />---<br />Also in The Drenai Saga: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577771334" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> ★★★★★ <br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305679740?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The King Beyond the Gate</a> ★★☆☆☆<br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2336920559" rel="nofollow noopener">Waylander</a> ★★★☆☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372503520" rel="nofollow noopener">Quest for Lost Heroes</a> ★★★★☆<br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407425852" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Realm of the Wolf</a> ★★★☆☆<br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2431984941?type=review#rating_170330840" rel="nofollow noopener">The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend</a> ★★★★☆<br />8. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517328446?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter Warriors</a> ★★★☆☆<br />9. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621547766" rel="nofollow noopener">Hero in the Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br />10. White Wolf RTC<br />11. The Swords of Night and Day RTC</span>

<div id="review_625875340" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/625875340" />
    <a title="Joe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3684279-joe"><img alt="Joe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588192445p2/3684279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/625875340?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe" href="/user/show/3684279-joe">Joe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3684279-joe?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer625875340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2179693108014379630">This was the last book in the Drenai Saga that I hadn’t read, so reading it was a very bittersweet experience. On the one hand, this one is just as good as all the other books in the series, and made me want to revisit Legend and some of the others. On the other hand, I knew that once I’d finished it, there wouldn’t be any more Drenai books left. So I took it slow for the first half, but naturally I finished it at a breathless late-night sprint a day or two later.<br/><br/>I’ve been thinking a lot lately </span>
  <span id="freeText2179693108014379630" style="display:none">This was the last book in the Drenai Saga that I hadn’t read, so reading it was a very bittersweet experience. On the one hand, this one is just as good as all the other books in the series, and made me want to revisit Legend and some of the others. On the other hand, I knew that once I’d finished it, there wouldn’t be any more Drenai books left. So I took it slow for the first half, but naturally I finished it at a breathless late-night sprint a day or two later.<br /><br />I’ve been thinking a lot lately about why I love David Gemmell’s books so much. There are many reasons, but I think the main reason is that his writing is honest. He strips away all the incidental stuff and gets right at the heart of the stuff that matters. He doesn’t pussyfoot around, either–if his characters do something despicable, he doesn’t make any excuses for them. He tells it like it is. This can make for a very brutal story, but it also makes for a very cathartic one.<br /><br />The other reason I love his books so much is because he does such a good job depicting raw, unrepressed manhood–not the stupid stuff like driving big cars and eating meat, but manning up and facing your greatest fears. It’s about friendship, and honor, and fighting with all of your strength for something you believe in. It’s about all that raw, pent-up energy we all have, that animal urge that drives us to competitive sports and first person shooters, and channeling it for a heroic cause.<br /><br />The craziest thing is that the fight itself is actually more important than whatever side the characters are fighting on. In this book, Druss is actually fighting to help bring about the rise of the Nadir khan who later <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[invades his homeland and kills him on the walls of Dros Delnoch.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> None of that matters, though, because Druss doesn’t fight with malice. For him, it’s all about fighting for something, not against something, and the battle itself is just as important as the victory. I don’t think I can put it better than this:<br /><br /> “Can we win here?” Sieben asked, as the shaman’s image began to fade.<br /><br /> “Winning and losing are entirely dependent on what you are fighting for,” answered <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Shaoshad <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. “All men here could die, yet you could still win. Or all men could live and you could lose. Fare you well, poet.”<br /><br />The best thing about David Gemmell’s books is the fact that none of the characters–not even the bad guys–are defined by their own evil. The Nadir are supposed to be the evil chaotic race of the Drenai universe, but when you come to understand what they’re fighting for, their hopes and dreams for a better future, you can really see what’s good in them. Likewise, the more civilized Gothir are kind of like the evil white men who want to put down the savages and keep them in their place, but there are good and honorable men among them too.<br /><br />And yet, even though the two sides clash, and good men die on both sides, it somehow isn’t tragic. That’s the crazy part. It’s almost like you can feel the characters salute each other as they die in a good cause, the way<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ulric gave Druss a proper funeral in Legend, even though the two were blood-sworn enemies. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> In David Gemmell’s world, honor and courage are more important than life or money. Everyone dies; dying well is more important than living without honor.<br /><br />This book is incredible. As I was reading it, I decided it was the best David Gemmell book I’ve ever read–which is something I do every time I read one of his books. I feel like I’m a better man for having read them. If he had written a hundred books in this series, I would happily read them all. The fact that there are no more new ones deeply saddens me, but I know I’ll revisit these stories again in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2179693108014379630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_813233155" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/813233155" />
    <a title="Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1760824-graham"><img alt="Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380743323p2/1760824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/813233155?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graham" href="/user/show/1760824-graham">Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552142526" href="/book/show/614003.The_Legend_of_Deathwalker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1760824-graham?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer813233155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4905126843374626530">A typically excellent fantasy novel by David Gemmell, something of a prequel of sorts to his first book, LEGEND. In fact, it has a couple of book-end chapters that directly link it to the events of that story, but the majority of the tale is set years previously.<br/><br/>This is one of the best Drenai novels. The plot is familiar, taking on yet another siege scenario, but the characters are among the most interesting yet and Gemmell makes full use of the opportunity to explore the various characters caug</span>
  <span id="freeText4905126843374626530" style="display:none">A typically excellent fantasy novel by David Gemmell, something of a prequel of sorts to his first book, LEGEND. In fact, it has a couple of book-end chapters that directly link it to the events of that story, but the majority of the tale is set years previously.<br /><br />This is one of the best Drenai novels. The plot is familiar, taking on yet another siege scenario, but the characters are among the most interesting yet and Gemmell makes full use of the opportunity to explore the various characters caught up in the events. There's a huge cast in this one and yet the character delineation is spot on to the degree that even the minor characters stay in the mind.<br /><br />Druss is, of course, head and shoulders above everyone else, but Sieben is particularly likeable here (as is his developing relationship with Niobe), and the characters of Gargan, Talisman, Nosta Khan, Kzun and Klay are all well drawn and interesting to read about. The action is splendid, invariably, but the philosophising and ruminations behind the story are even better. I particularly enjoyed the way that the bad-guy Nadir are the heroes here, allowing Gemmell to make the point that there is no good and evil, just men capable of great good and great evil on either side. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4905126843374626530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2287575526?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/66331236-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11743519-the-legend-of-deathwalker">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287575526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13551953852717073597">We find Druss battling the Nadir on the walls of Dros Delnoch and his mind goes back to the past and the events which led to him fighting beside the Nadir. Druss’s search for his wife Rowena led him to become the lethal fighter he turned into, more comfortable with violence and death than a peaceful life.<br/><br/>And so, circumstances send him on a quest for magic stones to save a friend’s life. Stones supposedly in a shrine right in the middle of Nadir territory. Perilous journey, anyone?<br/><br/>The book focuse</span>
  <span id="freeText13551953852717073597" style="display:none">We find Druss battling the Nadir on the walls of Dros Delnoch and his mind goes back to the past and the events which led to him fighting beside the Nadir. Druss’s search for his wife Rowena led him to become the lethal fighter he turned into, more comfortable with violence and death than a peaceful life.<br /><br />And so, circumstances send him on a quest for magic stones to save a friend’s life. Stones supposedly in a shrine right in the middle of Nadir territory. Perilous journey, anyone?<br /><br />The book focuses mainly on the Nadir. We get a deeper view into the Nadir and the kind of people they are. They are considered savages compared to the Drenai and their way of life is incomprehensible but the Drenai are no better. The way the Drenai treat the Nadir as less than human, the cruelty to their children is deplorable.<br /><br />We also find out the reason why the Nadir are so at odds and separated as a people. Oshikai Demon-Bane and Shut-sen’s story is heartbreaking.<br /><br />The one lesson prominent in all of David Gemmell’s books is that hate begets hate. The Nadir hate the Drenai and the Drenai hate them back. It’s a vicious circle that never ends.<br /><br />David Gemmell crafts an impressive plot with Druss and the Nadir fighting together for a noble cause. The conclusion for the Nadir was an impactful one but Druss’s quest? Ah, we’re given one of life’s biggest lessons here – how life never works out the way you want it to.<br /><br /><a href="https://nomadicworlds.wordpress.com/2018/03/09/book-review-the-legend-of-deathwalker-david-gemmell/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted on Blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13551953852717073597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1749949766" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1749949766" />
    <a title="Kostas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas"><img alt="Kostas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554812738p2/25638423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1749949766?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kostas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kostas" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas">Kostas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593037058" href="/book/show/2331390.The_Legend_of_Deathwalker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=heroic-fantasy">heroic-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1749949766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8412612120081219982">8/10<br/><br/>In ‘The Legend of Deathwalker’ Druss’s legendary cycle of adventures comes to an end as Gemmell takes us, once again, to the past, in a story of how Druss actually earns the title of the <i>Deathwalker</i> and also of how fate sends him at the siege of Dros Delnoch.<br/><br/>The story starts 30 years before <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_' title='Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Legend</a>
</i>, but after the main events of the <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/526071.The_First_Chronicles_of_Druss_the_Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___6_' title='The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend (The Drenai Saga, #6) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'>First Chronicles</a>
</i>, with Druss still trying to find himself in the world, along with Sieben, his most loyal friend and poet master.<br/>But when they get involved</span>
  <span id="freeText8412612120081219982" style="display:none">8/10<br /><br />In ‘The Legend of Deathwalker’ Druss’s legendary cycle of adventures comes to an end as Gemmell takes us, once again, to the past, in a story of how Druss actually earns the title of the <i>Deathwalker</i> and also of how fate sends him at the siege of Dros Delnoch.<br /><br />The story starts 30 years before <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_" title="Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a>
</i>, but after the main events of the <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/526071.The_First_Chronicles_of_Druss_the_Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___6_" title="The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend (The Drenai Saga, #6) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">First Chronicles</a>
</i>, with Druss still trying to find himself in the world, along with Sieben, his most loyal friend and poet master.<br />But when they get involved into Gothir's political intrigues, a friend’s life will come into mortal danger and they will have to travel to the land of the Nadir to seek the “Eyes of Alchazzar”; but that, will put them in a new, and even greater adventure.<br />However, it has been prophesied that when the “Eyes of Alchazzar” are found the “Uniter” will return, the “one” who will unite the Nadir tribes and will bring them back to glory. And so, Talisman, a Nadir warrior, having lived under the dominion of the Gothirs for many years he will, also, begin his own adventures for the “Eyes” and to try to unite the Nadir tribes.<br />Along the way though, he will discover that the paths of their fate, between him and the legendary Druss, might be much closer than he expected.<br /><br />I must to say that the story didn’t hold me as much as in the <i>First Chronicles</i>, perhaps because the story doesn’t focus so much on Druss, but I liked more Gemmell’s narrative in this one, as I think it flows better and has definitely better, and more balanced character development.<br />Of course, what makes this book even better is that Gemmell brought up, yet again, some very emotional moments from the characters, and especially near the end of the book, which I really liked and, I think, it changes the book as a whole.<br /><br />Overall, the book might not be one of Gemmell's greatest, but he gives a nice background for Druss and Ulric's past, and if you love Druss like me, well, you should not miss it.<br /><br /><br />Ελληνική κριτική:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Σε αυτό το βιβλίο ο κύκλος των περιπετειών του θρυλικού Druss φτάνει στο τέλος του με τον Gemmell να μας ταξιδεύει για άλλη μια φορά στο παρελθόν, σε μια ιστορία για το πώς κερδίζει τον τίτλο του Deathwalker αλλά και το πώς η μοίρα τον φέρνει στην μεγάλη μάχη του Dros Delnoch.<br /><br />Η ιστορία ξεκινάει 30 χρόνια πριν από το <i>Legend</i>, αλλά λίγο μετά τα βασικά γεγονότα του <i>First Chronicles</i>, με τον Druss να προσπαθεί ακόμα να βρει τον εαυτό του στον κόσμο, μαζί με τον Sieben, τον πιστό του φίλο και τροβαδούρο.<br />Όταν όμως μπλεχτούν ανάμεσα στις πολιτικές ίντριγκες των Gothir η ζωή ενός φίλου τους θα βρεθεί σε θανάσιμο κίνδυνο και θα πρέπει να ταξιδέψουν στην χώρα των Nadir για αναζητήσουν τα «Μάτια του Alchazzar» που όμως θα τους βάλει σε μια νέα, και μεγάλη περιπέτεια.<br />Όμως έχει προφητευτεί ότι όταν βρεθούν τα «Μάτια του Alchazzar» θα επιστρέψει ο «Uniter», ο «ένας» που θα ενώσει της φυλές των Nadir και θα τους φέρει πάλι στην δόξα. Έτσι ο Talisman, ένας Nadir πολεμιστής, έχοντας ζήσει κάτω από την εξουσία των Gothir για πολλά χρόνια θα ξεκινήσει και ο ίδιος την δική του περιπέτεια αναζήτησης για τα «Μάτια» αλλά και για να ενώσει τις φυλές των Nadir.<br />Στην πορεία όμως θα ανακαλύψει ότι οι δρόμοι της μοίρας του ίδιου με τον θρυλικό Druss είναι, ίσως, πιο κοντά απ’ όσο περίμενε.<br /><br />Η ιστορία πρέπει να πω δεν με κράτησε τόσο όσο στο <i>First Chronicles</i>, ίσως επειδή επικεντρώνεται αρκετά λιγότερο στον Druss, αλλά μου άρεσε περισσότερο η γραφή του Gemmell εδώ, μιας και πιστεύω ότι κυλάει πιο καλά και έχει σίγουρα καλύτερη, και πιο ισορροπημένη, ανάπτυξη στους χαρακτήρες.<br />Αυτό φυσικά που το κάνει ακόμα καλύτερο είναι ότι ο Gemmell βγάζει, για άλλη μια φορά, μερικές πολύ δυνατές συναισθηματικές στιγμές από τους χαρακτήρες, και ειδικά προς το τέλος του βιβλίου, πράγμα που μου άρεσε πολύ και, νομίζω, αλλάζει εντελώς την ίδια την ιστορία.<br /><br />Γενικά δεν θα το έλεγα από τα πιο δυνατά βιβλία του Gemmell αλλά δίνει ένα αρκετά ωραίο backround για τον Druss και τον Ulric, οπότε αν σας αρέσει ο Druss τότε σίγουρα δεν πρέπει να το χάσετε. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/383108904?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Filipa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Filipa" href="/user/show/4333754-filipa">Filipa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383108904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer998368225569173693">I do have a passion of David Gemmell books. He is simple in writing, concise in his battles, a great story teller and most of all , very human when creating his characters.<br/><br/>The Legend of Deathwalker brings us the story of Druss and the reason why he had the name of Deathwalker between the Nadir. It also brings the Nadir rising into the powerful army we have seen in the "Legend".<br/><br/>With a incredible simplicity, David Gemmell places Druss as a story teller to a young warrior about times long passed, w</span>
  <span id="freeText998368225569173693" style="display:none">I do have a passion of David Gemmell books. He is simple in writing, concise in his battles, a great story teller and most of all , very human when creating his characters.<br /><br />The Legend of Deathwalker brings us the story of Druss and the reason why he had the name of Deathwalker between the Nadir. It also brings the Nadir rising into the powerful army we have seen in the "Legend".<br /><br />With a incredible simplicity, David Gemmell places Druss as a story teller to a young warrior about times long passed, when he was in his thirties going to the Games as a fist fighter. From that moment forward, anything and everything happened. <br /><br />I don't like to make big reviews on David Gemmell books because I tend to make spoils. And if one thing is important when reading his books is the details.<br /><br />So, go and read. Really. It will be worth your time. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8321720839075952441">David Gemmell could have written about Druss (and Sieben) doing groceries and baking cakes and I would have enjoyed it. David Gemmell's style is one that I can't get tired of, even though I have always believed that he wrote the same book over and over again.   <span id="freeText8321720839075952441" style="display:none">David Gemmell could have written about Druss (and Sieben) doing groceries and baking cakes and I would have enjoyed it. David Gemmell's style is one that I can't get tired of, even though I have always believed that he wrote the same book over and over again. "The Legend of the Deathwalker" is not as good as the Rigante series or the first two about Troy, but it still has all the ingredients of the his novels (a little bit of talk about philosophy, endings a little bit abrupt, characters that are fleshed out in two lines, and probably some of the best heroes ever written about. You can stand behind Druss, even if you don't agree with him, and his search for the healing stones and his way of life is one to respect. As always with Gemmell, fun to read from beginning to end!<br /><br />8</span>

<div id="review_3218860847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3218860847" />
    <a title="John Adams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58175327-john-adams"><img alt="John Adams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496479523p2/58175327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3218860847?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Adams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Adams" href="/user/show/58175327-john-adams">John Adams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58175327-john-adams?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3218860847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10200271200439255087">The Legend of Deathwalker by David Gemmell<br/><br/><br/>Featuring Gemmell's legendary creation Druss the Axe, this is 'epic fantasy with a side-serving of romance' at its best.<br/><br/>During the decades of his career, Druss the Axe became one of Gemmell's best-known creations, appearing in many novels and novellas over the years, either as a central character or as a supporting member of a wider cast.<br/><br/>Here we find Druss in later life after his successful quest to rescue his wife Rowena from the slavers who stole her a</span>
  <span id="freeText10200271200439255087" style="display:none">The Legend of Deathwalker by David Gemmell<br /><br /><br />Featuring Gemmell's legendary creation Druss the Axe, this is 'epic fantasy with a side-serving of romance' at its best.<br /><br />During the decades of his career, Druss the Axe became one of Gemmell's best-known creations, appearing in many novels and novellas over the years, either as a central character or as a supporting member of a wider cast.<br /><br />Here we find Druss in later life after his successful quest to rescue his wife Rowena from the slavers who stole her away from their farmstead, sparking a lengthy and complex search for her by her stricken husband. Druss is here found riding with poet-sidekick Sieben to seek the Eyes of Alchazzar.<br /><br />Simultaneously, young general Talisman is charged with safely delivered Zhusai, the beautiful granddaughter of Chiatze leader Chorin-Tsu to her new husband, the fabled Uniter with violet eyes who will bring the Nadir peoples together in peace and end the perennial fighting against the Gothir.<br /><br />This book is pure quest epic, and Talisman and Zhusai's journey is both emotional (falling in love with each other) and physical, as they search for the longlost but never forgotten Eyes. These jewels are fabled to light the path to the Uniter, who at the start of the novel has not yet been identified but whose revealing is sensed to be imminent.<br /><br />Druss and Sieben are also searching for the Eyes, hoping to save wounded adversary Klay. There are moments when the unlikely presence of Druss in this scenario feels a little constructed, but diehard fans of Gemmell's writing like me require no excuse to spend more time in Druss's company.<br /><br />This isn't the longest book in a genre notable for door-wedge novels that run to many hundreds of thousands of words. There is really just the one plot strand, and although it is deftly wielded through physical action and emotional development the story is quite straightforward. That's no bad thing - it gives plenty of space for the love story that lies at the heart of most Gemmell novels, and which is part of the satisfying nature of the plot arc here.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10200271200439255087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2862508624" />
    <a title="Brian Turner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32091109-brian-turner"><img alt="Brian Turner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476364278p2/32091109.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2862508624?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Turner" href="/user/show/32091109-brian-turner">Brian Turner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32091109-brian-turner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2862508624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4141565233404684034">I did like this book - the characters and dialogue were strong, the plot was well done, and all in all it would have been a great book if it stood by itself. <br/><br/>The trouble was, I couldn't shake the feeling of <i>deja vu</i>: a group of people hold up among ruins in an old building in a wasteland, ready to resist a violent siege by superior forces. <br/><br/>I know Gemmell has a habit of reusing the same formula but here it just seemed so blatant, which is a shame because this is one of the stronger Drenai books I'</span>
  <span id="freeText4141565233404684034" style="display:none">I did like this book - the characters and dialogue were strong, the plot was well done, and all in all it would have been a great book if it stood by itself. <br /><br />The trouble was, I couldn't shake the feeling of <i>deja vu</i>: a group of people hold up among ruins in an old building in a wasteland, ready to resist a violent siege by superior forces. <br /><br />I know Gemmell has a habit of reusing the same formula but here it just seemed so blatant, which is a shame because this is one of the stronger Drenai books I've read so far but sense of familiarity managed to spoil something of the enjoyment.<br /><br />Otherwise, it was interesting to see Gemmell revisit the past to flesh out the Drenai world-building, not least character histories and how they connected. And though it was a good idea and well executed, I struggled to feel convinced. <br /><br />In the end there's something of the whiff of <i>Rogue One</i> about this - an interesting but unnecessary story. The difference being, this book is a much more worthwhile use of time. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4141565233404684034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I chose this series as part f my reading challenge for this year, and as a buddy read with one of my colleagues. Even though the first book in the series was released in 1984 (and the latest in 2000) the series has pretty much stood the test of time.   <span id="freeText10139882979598060093" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />I have really enjoyed revisiting this book/series. I chose this series as part f my reading challenge for this year, and as a buddy read with one of my colleagues. Even though the first book in the series was released in 1984 (and the latest in 2000) the series has pretty much stood the test of time. It is a fantastic action adventure fantasy- with superb characters and brilliant world building, which brings the whole story/series to life.<br />I have fond memories of discovering this series and excitedly awaiting each new instalment. My reading buddy hadn’t read the series before, but has also enjoyed discovering David Gemmell’s work/s.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1564520913" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1564520913" />
    <a title="Fari Manonose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31556971-fari-manonose"><img alt="Fari Manonose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467315779p2/31556971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1564520913?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fari Manonose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fari Manonose" href="/user/show/31556971-fari-manonose">Fari Manonose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1564520913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17930280048212661618">We once again go on an adventure with Druss the Legend, to find out how he got the name Deathwalker, among the Nadir. David Gemmel’s writing style as always is amazing. <b>He was especially great at writing characters though</b>. Although his heroes and their love interests always seem to have repetitive characteristics but I guess it follows that Heroes will have similar traits that make them heroes, and that the women they love would also share similar traits. His heroes aren’t identical though, they</span>
  <span id="freeText17930280048212661618" style="display:none">We once again go on an adventure with Druss the Legend, to find out how he got the name Deathwalker, among the Nadir. David Gemmel’s writing style as always is amazing. <b>He was especially great at writing characters though</b>. Although his heroes and their love interests always seem to have repetitive characteristics but I guess it follows that Heroes will have similar traits that make them heroes, and that the women they love would also share similar traits. His heroes aren’t identical though, they are just similar. Other than that he created the most unique lovable characters. If they weren’t lovable he made (makes?) you root for and love them. The best part of Gemmel’s writing are the characters I think.<br><br>Main themes in the book were the question of morality, on one hand we have someone who says sacrifice the few,save the many they see things in shades of grey. On the other hand was Druss, who saw things in black and white, and Gemmel in this book puts forward a good argument for this point of view, which is unconventional as most people support the shades of grey point of view. One of the major themes which is evident throughout the series is that of hope. Knowing that there is always a chance of success no matter how bad the odds. <br><br><b>What I liked:</b><br><br>&gt;I’ve always liked that the series is not in a chronological order, It’s probably been done before but for me this is a new experience and I find it really interesting and unique. <br>&gt;Sieben <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[finally found love!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>&gt;The way David Gemmel writes even the smallest characters, you never know if you will only see a character once or if they will become a major player because he gives each of them a history, hopes and dreams or their lack of them. It’s true to life though, because all those people that are extras in our lives are main actors in their own, they aren’t just ‘the bus driver’ or ‘the guy on a bicycle. <br>&gt;<b>The twist ending!!!</b> I did not see that coming. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I thought Ulric would be talisman’s son or something! This is even what I wrote about talisman: <br><i>It seems to me that talisman, like Waylander is a small catalyst who is to facilitate a big reaction, the coming of the uniter. People might not sing about him, but he is one of the all important people in the background, who allow major events to happen i.e the coming of the uniter. </i> <br>Who knew he would be Ulric?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>What I didn’t like</b><br><br>&gt;Okay, the books in this series have had many things in common and it’s becoming a bit repetitive<br>1.	A siege.<br>2.	Somehow a Nadir and a Drenai is involved.<br>3.	The side Gemmel makes us root for has the odds against them.<br>4.	Somehow, they prevail.<br>5.	Noone we really love dies, and if they do, it’s such a glorious death that we’re not too sad to let them go.<br><br>&gt;Like I said, I like how the books aren’t in their chronological order but it takes away from the experience somehow. Like for Druss, <b>I don’t fear for his life because I know the exact moment he dies, I know the uniter will come for the Nadir, I know all this because I have read the preceding books.<b></b><br><br> This book was great. Like all David Gemmel books. <br><b>Favourite Quote:</b><br><blockquote>'You mock politics,' he said softly. 'You sneer at diplomacy. But how do <br>you think we hold the world at peace? I'll tell you, Sieben. Men like me travel to places like this, and <br>we're fed those horse-turd cakes of yours. And we smile, and we say how nourishing they are. We <br>move in the space between other men's egos, massaging them as we walk. We do this not for gain, <br>but for peace and prosperity. We do it so that Drenai farmers, merchants, clerics and labourers can <br>raise their families in peace. Druss is a hero; he can enjoy the luxury of living his own life and <br>speaking his own truths. Diplomats cannot.</blockquote>
<br><br>My face at the end of this book<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456844410ra/18284080.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17930280048212661618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/725491763?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/19121404-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer725491763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15593918214956472002">I liked this book although it was hard to follow as it is the 7th in a series that I have read no other books.It took me awhile to get all the characters figured out and all the different peoples. <br/>The story starts in a fight,Druss the legend is awaiting the Nadir to attack yet again. He is an older warrior, of around 50 or 60 and he has a young man next to him. As it turns out Dros is telling the young man his story of how he got his name "Deathwalker". He had been going to the games but had got</span>
  <span id="freeText15593918214956472002" style="display:none">I liked this book although it was hard to follow as it is the 7th in a series that I have read no other books.It took me awhile to get all the characters figured out and all the different peoples. <br />The story starts in a fight,Druss the legend is awaiting the Nadir to attack yet again. He is an older warrior, of around 50 or 60 and he has a young man next to him. As it turns out Dros is telling the young man his story of how he got his name "Deathwalker". He had been going to the games but had gotten into a fight with his countries "fighter" for the games.Druss beat the fighter so badly he could no longer compete so Druss took his place. He did a great job too getting into the final with relative ease. However the King of the land in which the games were being held didn't want to lose the games so he sent warriors to mame Druss. It didn't work the warriors ended up mortally wounding Drusses opponant. Druss had just had his life saved by this man, who lay before Druss mortally wounded. His name was Klay and they took him to a hospice to die. Druss was told by a Shamen, who appeared to him in a bar, that if he found the Eyes of Alchazaar he could heal his friend.The book is the story of Druss trying to find the jewels, fighting the bad guys, the people of Gothir, in this case, and helping the Nadir, whom he is now fighting against, to keep there sacred grounds sacred!<br />The book does have a lot of action in it but it also can be quite confusing if you haven't read the books that came before it I am assuming. </span>

<div id="review_373551469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/373551469" />
    <a title="Andrea Bampi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10919735-andrea-bampi"><img alt="Andrea Bampi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344429385p2/10919735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/373551469?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1262870153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11231054355723318222"><u>The Legend of Deathwalker (Drenai Saga, #7)</u> tells the story of how Druss gets his Nadir name of Deathwalker. It also tells of how Ulrech is created - which explains Druss's funeral in the very first Drenai Saga novel - and how Sieben finally found his ability to love which, it should be noted, is different than his ability to be a lov<b>er</b> which we already knew him capable of.<br/><br/>Missing is Rowena.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18299177426380392025">This is book number 7 in the series. By now, I thought I would find the narrative repetitive and slightly tiresome. <br/>That is not the case. David Gemmell continues to create original fiction story lines and the characters in his books display depth and character.<br/>I found myself immersed in this particular work to the extent that sadness and excitement were evoked as the pages flowed. The characters lives and struggles became important to me.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13181464998923754428">This is another <i>Druss the Legend</i> novel. The story revolves mostly around Druss telling an anecdote to a young soldier during the events that happen in <u>Legend</u>. Focused mostly on Druss's time with the Nadir, it follows the main pattern of many of the other books in the Drenai Saga.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3410386905" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3410386905" />
    <a title="Thomas Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/116268158-thomas-robert"><img alt="Thomas Robert" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3410386905?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Robert" href="/user/show/116268158-thomas-robert">Thomas Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3410386905&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3410386905" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5036461660645711054">I enjoyed this book more than any of the other six Drenai Saga novels which came before it. Much as ‘The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend’ (the previous instalment) marked a step up in terms of scale and complexity, ‘The Legend of Deathwalker’ felt like yet another step forward - this time in the way of depth. To me, this felt altogether a more vivid; richer, and more sophisticated work than any of the previous books. Unfortunately however, I thought that Gemmell still made a few vexing blun</span>
  <span id="freeText5036461660645711054" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book more than any of the other six Drenai Saga novels which came before it. Much as ‘The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend’ (the previous instalment) marked a step up in terms of scale and complexity, ‘The Legend of Deathwalker’ felt like yet another step forward - this time in the way of depth. To me, this felt altogether a more vivid; richer, and more sophisticated work than any of the previous books. Unfortunately however, I thought that Gemmell still made a few vexing blunders, which detracted somewhat from my enjoyment of what was otherwise a really good book; I will start with the blunders:<br /><br />1. Gemmell spends the first 100 pages, skilfully building a high level of anticipation and suspense around a planned arena fight, which, due to a sudden attack on one of the protagonists, simply doesn’t take place at all.<br /><br /> Whilst, as it pans out, this turn of events acts as the catalyst for the main story to begin, I still don’t feel it was necessary for things to happen in this way, and I remember feeling distinctly disappointed that the bout never took place.<br /><br />2. David ‘Siege’ Gemmell, bogs us down in - you guessed it - another siege... I think, of the seven Drenai Saga books which I have now read, there was only one which did not involve the main characters being involved in a defensive siege of some description... Now don’t get me wrong - there’s nothing intrinsically unreasonable about including a siege in a heroic fantasy novel; it just gets a little repetitive that’s all!<br /><br />3. Just like in ‘Legend,’ the author employs a cheap, Deus Ex Machina plot device to bring things to a close; which in my mind, aside from being wholly unnecessary, robs what should be a glorious and triumphant moment, of, well... All its glory, and triumph.<br /><br />On the positive side: <br /><br /> As in the previous book (The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend) there are a myriad of side characters, which - as I remarked when reviewing that book, makes a marked improvement over the rather sparse, prosaic and linear feel of the first five books. Unlike in ‘The First Chronicles of Druss’ however, where many of our new army of side characters seemed to be sketched a little vaguely, and came across as somewhat forgettable cardboard cutouts - in this instalment, all of our characters come complete with unique personal histories and compelling backstories, leaving the whole novel feeling richer, deeper and more mature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5036461660645711054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1987674593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987674593" />
    <a title="Tiberiu Pana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44241978-tiberiu-pana"><img alt="Tiberiu Pana" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1987674593?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiberiu Pana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiberiu Pana" href="/user/show/44241978-tiberiu-pana">Tiberiu Pana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44241978-tiberiu-pana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1987674593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13114114752146402096">My oh my!<br/><br/>First thing first, I have to state that I've read David Gemmell's Troy trilogy, Legend and all the books in the Drenai saga that were before this one from a chronological point of view.<br/>I wish now I haven't rated some of them as high as I did, only because this one is a rare gem.<br/><br/>The Legend of Deathwalker resembles the third one in the Waylander trilogy in the fact that even though the main character is Druss and the actions evolves around him, the reader's attention will most likely go t</span>
  <span id="freeText13114114752146402096" style="display:none">My oh my!<br /><br />First thing first, I have to state that I've read David Gemmell's Troy trilogy, Legend and all the books in the Drenai saga that were before this one from a chronological point of view.<br />I wish now I haven't rated some of them as high as I did, only because this one is a rare gem.<br /><br />The Legend of Deathwalker resembles the third one in the Waylander trilogy in the fact that even though the main character is Druss and the actions evolves around him, the reader's attention will most likely go towards the secondary characters...and here the similarities stop.<br /><br />Character work is spot on as usual in Gemmell's works, but if before you could have decided early on who you like and who you hate...well now you'll go through a roller coaster of feelings towards some of the characters. This plus a intricate scenario, that is just the best so far in the Drenai saga (and I don't know why I have the feeling I won't see a better one throughout the series), makes this book a rare find.<br /><br />This is even a hidden gem for even Druss himself, if I can say that! If you're familiar with the saga, you'd heard of Sieben, the saga master, Druss's loyal companian. Well, even though he's by the Legend's side throughout the action, he misses some of it (you'll have to find out how). Thus Deathwalkers greatest achievement will remain unsung...</span>
  <a data-text-id="13114114752146402096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3568571363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3568571363" />
    <a title="Keith Warren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33816288-keith-warren"><img alt="Keith Warren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590373936p2/33816288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3568571363?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keith Warren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keith Warren" href="/user/show/33816288-keith-warren">Keith Warren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3568571363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7360933682758598718">Absolute masterpiece. David Gemmell was truly a master of the craft. These last two Druss novels are some of the most enjoyable books I've read this year. This one especially.<br/><br/>Druss really is a great character of indomitable spirit, his sense of honour is again so inspiring. I can't say too much without spoilers but this book filled me with a proper bittersweet feeling that's for sure. Him and Sieben are a great duo. Their buddy relationship is in full force again here. This book did a better job</span>
  <span id="freeText7360933682758598718" style="display:none">Absolute masterpiece. David Gemmell was truly a master of the craft. These last two Druss novels are some of the most enjoyable books I've read this year. This one especially.<br /><br />Druss really is a great character of indomitable spirit, his sense of honour is again so inspiring. I can't say too much without spoilers but this book filled me with a proper bittersweet feeling that's for sure. Him and Sieben are a great duo. Their buddy relationship is in full force again here. This book did a better job of making me like Sieben as a character.<br /><br />There's a few story lines happening all at once and you gotta pay attention. This book fills in a lot of gaps from Legend and First Chronicles. It also takes place a few years after he rescues Rowena, so in between events of First Chronicles. <br /><br />I adore the hell out of this book, I spent at least 30 min afterwards just thinking about it. I nearly freaking cried. Goddamn it.<br /><br />10/10 - Second only to The King Beyond the Gate in the Drenai series for me.<br /><br />See this and other reviews + my own average stories at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://keithwarrenwriter.com">https://keithwarrenwriter.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7360933682758598718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cIHuL3VTwN0o4z7oWQ7wa5glFpF/PDHy6VsOpXzncKEKTmLrIsC8xoSo1xJC6XLbdWQmyxpRnALENYCPy0Aclg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+jNKyh1RZ7mv8X+k89XpR0kIl7SDqwZkJF/7/2JrdDWA/MYOSsIbogO6ll7oMmv3pEmn7ubGq5QJMXXV1cwYAg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11050923219163919380">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sel</span>
  <span id="freeText11050923219163919380" style="display:none">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sell worldwide.</span>
